                           </msub>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\rm{Ni}} + 3/2{\rm{KB}}{{\rm{i}}}_2-3/2{{\rm{K}}}^ + - 3/2{{\rm{e}}}^ - \to {\rm{NiB}}{{\rm{i}}}_3\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(5)</span></div>
         </div>
         
         <p>According to this reaction mechanism, the K-storage of the NiBi<sub>3</sub> possesses one potential plateau during potassiation and two potential plateaus during depotassition, with a theoretical specific capacity of 351.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
         
         <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305551-fig-0007">7c</a> exhibits the in situ EIS spectra evolution of the NiBi<sub>3</sub> anode of the first cycle. The <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> gradually decreased from 17.9 to 11.1 Ω with the K insertion, indicating that the generated Ni and K<sub>3</sub>Bi phases are helpful for the charge transfer. After being charged back to 1.8&nbsp;V, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> increased back to 13.3 Ω due to the rebuild of NiBi<sub>3</sub> and the disappearance of the K<sub>3</sub>Bi and KBi<sub>2</sub> phases. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305551-fig-0007">7d</a> presents the morphology change of the NiBi<sub>3</sub> electrode during cycling. Similar to the morphology change during Na-storage, the macro-sized NiBi<sub>3</sub> particle transform into nano-sized porous structure after 5 cycles, and then became more porous after 10 and 50 cycles with the particle size reduction. The formation of the nanoporous structure is beneficial for alleviating volume expansion during cycling. In addition, the EDS mapping of the NiBi<sub>3</sub> particle after 50 cycling shows that the Ni and Bi are still uniformly distributed, indicating the superior reversibility of the NiBi<sub>3</sub> for K-storage (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305551-fig-0007">7e</a>).</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202305551-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202305551-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>Quasi-1D structured NiBi<sub>3</sub> has been successfully synthesized by combining layer-structured Bi and Ni to develop a novel anode for Na/K-ion storage. Benefiting from the quasi-1D structure superiority, the NiBi<sub>3</sub> exhibits metallic conductivity and 3D Na/K-ion diffusion pathways. When used as anode materials for Na/K ion storage, the NiBi<sub>3</sub> anode delivers an excellent capacity retention of 94.1% (332 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) after 15&nbsp;000 cycles for Na-storage and a high ICE of 93.4% for K-storage. Ex situ XRD analysis reveals that the NiBi<sub>3</sub> undergoes a symmetric reaction mechanism of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/8c0cc59a-62c9-49de-a141-c0d79bfcae51/adma202305551-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202305551:adma202305551-math-0006" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202305551-math-0006.png">
               <semantics>
                  <mrow>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>NiBi</mi>
                        <mn>3</mn>
                     </msub>
                     <mo>⇌</mo>
                     <mi>Ni</mi>
                     <mo>+</mo>
                     <mi>NaBi</mi>
                     <mo>+</mo>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>Na</mi>
                        <mn>3</mn>
                     </msub>
                     <mi>Bi</mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{NiBi}}_{3}\rightleftharpoons \mathrm{Ni}+\mathrm{NaBi}+{\mathrm{Na}}_{3}\mathrm{Bi}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> for Na-storage and an asymmetric reaction mechanism of <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/c38e07d1-d840-4443-b554-054bbd396b0f/adma202305551-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202305551:adma202305551-math-0007" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202305551-math-0007.png">
               <semantics>
                  <mrow>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>NiBi</mi>
                        <mn>3</mn>
                     </msub>
                     <mo>→</mo>
                     <mi>Ni</mi>
                     <mo>+</mo>
                     <msub>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi>
                        <mn>3</mn>
                     </msub>
                     <mi>Bi</mi>
                     <mo>→</mo>
                     <mi>Ni</mi>
                     <mo>+</mo>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>KBi</mi>
                        <mn>2</mn>
                     </msub>
                     <mo>→</mo>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>NiBi</mi>
                        <mn>3</mn>
                     </msub>
                  </mrow>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{NiBi}}_{3}\to \mathrm{Ni}+{\mathrm{K}}_{3}\mathrm{Bi}\to \mathrm{Ni}+{\mathrm{KBi}}_{2}\to {\mathrm{NiBi}}_{3}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math> for K-storage. These two reactions are highly reversible due to the low formation energy of the NiBi<sub>3</sub>. In addition, ex situ SEM investigation reveals that the NiBi<sub>3</sub> electrode can spontaneously transform to the nanoporous structure during cycling, which accommodating the volume expansion and shortening the transport path of Na/K-ions. This study provides a new strategy for designing novel anode materials for Na/K-ion batteries.</p>
         </section>
